18tn (62:12) Or "the redeemed of the LORD."
1sn (63:1) Edom is here an archetype for the LORD's enemies. See 34:5.
2tn (63:1) Heb "[in] bright red garments, from Bozrah."
3tn (63:1) The interrogative particle is understood by ellipsis; note the first line of the verse.
4tn (63:1) Heb "honored in his clothing."
5tc (63:1) The Hebrew text has hux, which means "stoop, bend" (51:14). The translation assumes an emendation to dux, "march" (see BDB 858).
6tn (63:1) Heb "I, [the one] speaking in vindication [or, "righteousness"], great to deliver."
7tn (63:2) Heb "and your garments like one who treads in a vat?"
8sn (63:3) Nations, headed by Edom, are the object of the LORD's anger (see v. 6). He compares military slaughter to stomping on grapes in a vat.
9tn (63:3) For discussion of the difficult verb form, see HALOT 170. Perhaps the form is mixed, combining the first person forms of the imperfect (note the alef prefix) and perfect (note the yt- ending).
10tn (63:4) Heb "for the day of vengeance was in my heart, and the year of my revenge came." The term ylwag is sometimes translated here "my redemption," for the verbal root lag often means "deliver, buy back." A la@G{, "kinsman-redeemer," was responsible for protecting the extended family's interests, often by redeeming property that had been sold outside the family. However, the responsibilities of a la@G{ extended beyond financial concerns. He was also responsible for avenging the shed blood of a family member (see Num 35:19-27; Deut 19:6-12). In Isa 63:4, where vengeance is a prominent theme (note the previous line), it is probably this function of the family protector that is in view. The LORD pictures himself as a blood avenger who waits for the day of vengeance to arrive and then springs into action.
11sn (63:5) See Isa 59:16 for similar language.
12tn (63:5) Heb "and my anger, it supported me."
13sn (63:6) See Isa 49:26 and 51:23 for similar imagery.
14tn (63:6) Heb "and I brought down to the ground their juice." "Juice" refers to their blood (see v. 3).
15tn (63:7) Heb "according to all which."
16tn (63:7) Heb "greatness of goodness to the house of Israel which he did for them."
17tn (63:7) Heb "according to."
18tn (63:8) Heb "children [who] do not act deceitfully." Here the verb refers to covenantal loyalty.
19tn (63:9) Heb "in all their distress, there was distress to him" (reading ol with the margin/Qere).
20tn (63:9) Heb "the messenger [or, "angel"] of his face."
sn (63:9) This may refer to the "angel of God" mentioned in Exod 14:19, who in turn may be identical to the divine "presence" (literally, "face") referred to in Exod 33:14-15 and Deut 4:37. Here in Isa 63 this messenger may be equated with God's "holy Spirit" (see vv. 10-11) and "the Spirit of the LORD" (v. 14). See also Ps 139:7, where God's "Spirit" seems to be equated with his "presence" (literally, "face") in the synonymous parallelistic structure.
21tn (63:9) Or, "redeemed, delivered."
22tn (63:9) Heb "all the days of antiquity."
23tn (63:10) Or, "grieved, hurt the feelings of."
24sn (63:10) The phrase "holy Spirit" occurs in the OT only here (in v. 11 as well) and in Ps 51:11 (ET = v. 13 HT), where it is associated with the divine presence.
25tn (63:11) Heb "and he remembered the days of antiquity, Moses, his people." The syntax of the statement is unclear. The translation assumes that "his people" is the subject of the verb "remembered." If original, "Moses" is in apposition to "the days of antiquity," more precisely identifying the time period referred to. However, the syntactical awkwardness suggests that "Moses" may have been an early marginal note (perhaps identifying "the shepherd of his flock" two lines later) that has worked its way into the text.
26tn (63:11) The Hebrew text has a plural form, which if retained and taken as a numerical plural, would probably refer to Moses, Aaron, and the Israelite tribal leaders at the time of the Exodus. Most prefer to emend the form to the singular (hur) and understand this as a reference just to Moses.
27sn (63:11) See the note at v. 10.
28tn (63:12) Heb "who caused to go at the right hand of Moses the arm of his splendor."
29tn (63:12) Heb "making for himself a lasting name."
30tn (63:13) Heb "in the desert [or, "steppe"]."
31tn (63:14) The words "to graze" are supplied in the translation for clarification.
32tn (63:14) Or, "so, thus."
33tn (63:14) Heb "making for yourself a majestic name."
34tn (63:15) This probably refers to his zeal for his people, which motivates him to angrily strike out against their enemies.
35tn (63:15) The Hebrew text reads literally, "the agitation of your intestines and your compassion to me they are held back." The phrase "agitation of your intestines" is metonymic, referring to the way in which one's nervous system reacts when one feels pity and compassion toward another. yla, "to me," is awkward in this context, where the speaker represents the nation and, following the introduction (see v. 7), utilizes first person plural forms. The translation assumes an emendation to the negative particle la^. This also necessitates emending the following verb form (which is a plural perfect) to a singular jussive (qpatt). The Hitpael of qpa also occurs in 42:14.
36tn (63:16) Heb "our protector [or, "redeemer"] from antiquity [is] your name."
37tn (63:17) Some suggest a tolerative use of the Hiphil here, "[why do] you allow us to stray?" Though the Hiphil of hut appears to be tolerative in Jer 50:6, elsewhere it is preferable or necessary to take it as causative. See Isa 3:12; 9:15; and 30:28, as well as Gen 20:13; 2 Kgs 21:9; Job 12:24-25; Prov 12:26; Jer 23:13, 32; Hos 4:12; Amos 2:4; Mic 3:5.
38tn (63:17) This probably refers to God's commands.
39tn (63:17) Heb "[Why do] you harden our heart[s] so as not to fear you." The interrogative particle is understood by ellipsis (note the preceding line).
sn (63:17) How direct this hardening is, one cannot be sure. The speaker may envision direct involvement on the LORD's part. The LORD has brought the exile as judgment for the nation's sin and now he continues to keep them at arm's length by blinding them spiritually. The second half of 64:7 (ET) might support this, though the precise reading of the final verb is uncertain. On the other hand, the idiom of lament is sometimes ironic and hyperbolically deterministic. For example, Naomi lamented that Shaddai was directly opposing her and bringing her calamity (Ruth 1:20-21), while the author of Ps 88 directly attributes his horrible suffering and loneliness to God (see especially vv. 6-8, 16-18). Both individuals make little, if any, room for intermediate causes or the principle of sin and death which ravages the human race. In the same way, the speaker in Isa 63:17 (who evidences great spiritual sensitivity and is anything but "hardened") may be referring to the hardships of exile, which discouraged and even embittered the people, causing many of them to retreat from their Yahwistic faith. In this case, the "hardening" in view is more indirect and can be lifted by the LORD's intervention. Whether the hardening here is indirect or direct, it is important to recognize that the speaker sees it as one of the effects of rebellion against the LORD (note especially 64:5-6).
40tn (63:18) Or, "holy."
41tn (63:18) Heb "for a short time they had a possession, the people of your holiness."
42tn (63:18) Heb "your adversaries stomped on."
43tn (63:19) Heb "we were from antiquity" (see v. 16). The collocation <lwu + /m + hyh occurs only here.
44tn (63:19) Heb "you did not rule them, your name was not called over them." The expression "the name is called over" indicates ownership; see the note at 4:1. As these two lines stand they are very difficult to interpret. They appear to be stating that the adversaries just mentioned in v. 18 have not been subject to the LORD's rule in the past, perhaps explaining why they could commit the atrocity described in v. 18b.
1sn (63:19) In the Hebrew text (BHS) the chapter division occurs in a different place from the English Bible: 64:1 ET = 63:19b HT, and 64:2-12 ET = 64:1-11 HT. Beginning with 65:1 the verse numbers in the English Bible and the Hebrew Bible are again the same.
2tn (63:19) Or "the heavens." The same Hebrew term, <y]m^v* (v*m^y]<), may be translated "heavens" or "sky" depending on the context.
3tn (63:19) Or, "quake." wlzn is from the verbal root llz, "quake" (see HALOT 272). Perhaps there is a verbal allusion to Judg 5:5, the only other passage where this verb occurs. In that passage the poet tells how the LORD's appearance to do battle caused the mountains to shake.
4tn (64:1) Heb "to make known your name to your adversaries." Perhaps the infinitive construct with preposition -l= should be construed with "come down" in v. 1a, or subordinated to the following line: "To make known your name to your adversaries, let the nations shake from before you."
5tn (64:3) Heb "[for which] we were not waiting."
6tn (64:3) See the note at v. 1.
7tn (64:4) Heb "from ancient times they have not heard, they have not listened."
8tn (64:5) Heb "meet [with kindness]."
9tn (64:5) Heb "the one who rejoices and does righteousness."
10tn (64:5) Heb "in your ways they remember you."
11tc (64:5) The Hebrew text reads literally, "look, you were angry and we sinned against them continually [or perhaps, "in ancient times"] and we were delivered." The statement makes little sense as it stands. The first vav consecutive ("and we sinned") must introduce an explanatory clause here (see Num 1:48 and Isa 39:1 for other examples of this relatively rare use of the vav consecutive). The final verb makes no sense in this context--God's anger at their sin resulted in judgment, not deliverance. The translation above assumes an emendation to uvrnw, "and we were evil."
12tn (64:6) Heb "and like a garment of menstruation [are] all our righteous acts."
13tn (64:7) Or, "calls out in."
14tn (64:7) Or, "rouses himself."
15tn (64:7) Heb "for you have hidden your face from us."
16tc (64:7) The Hebrew text reads literally, "and you caused us to melt in the hand of our sin." The verb Wng}WmT=w~ is a Qal preterite 2ms with a 1cpl suffix from the root gWm, "melt." However, elsewhere the Qal of this verb is intransitive. If the verbal root gWm is retained here, the form should be emended to a Polel pattern (Wng}g+m)T=w~). The translation assumes an emendation to Wnn}G+m^T=w~, "and you handed us over." This form is a Piel preterite 2ms with a 1cpl suffix from the verbal root /G}m!, "hand over, surrender" (see HALOT 545, and BDB 171). The point is that God has abandoned them to their sinful ways and no longer seeks reconciliation.
17tn (64:8) On the force of htuw here, see HALOT 902.
18tn (64:8) Heb "the work of your hand."
19tn (64:9) Heb "do not remember sin continually."
20tn (64:9) Heb "Look, gaze at your people, all of us." Another option is to translate, "Take a good look! We are all your people."
21tn (64:10) Heb "holy."
22tn (64:11) Heb "our source of pride."
23tn (64:11) Or, "all that we valued has become a ruin."
24tn (64:12) Heb "because of these."
1tn (65:1) Heb "I allowed myself to be sought by those who did not ask."
2tn (65:1) Heb "I allowed myself to be found by those who did not seek."
3tn (65:1) Heb "call out in."
4tn (65:2) Heb "who walked [in] the way that is not good, after their thoughts."
5tn (65:3) Heb "the people who provoke me to anger to my face continually."
6tn (65:3) Or, "gardens."
7tn (65:3) Or, perhaps, "on tiles."
8sn (65:4) Perhaps the worship of underworld deities or dead spirits is in view.
9tn (65:4) The Hebrew text reads literally, "and in the watches they spend the night." Some understand <yrwxn as referring to "secret places" or "caves," while others emend the text to <yrx /yb, "between the rocky cliffs."
10tn (65:4) Heb "the flesh of the pig."
11tc (65:4) The marginal reading (Qere), supported by 1QIsa, reads qrm, "broth," while the consonantal text (Kethib) has qrp, "fragment."
12tn (65:6) Heb "Look, it is written before me."
13tn (65:6) Heb "I will pay back into their lap."
14tn (65:7) Heb "fathers'."
15tn (65:7) Or, perhaps, "taunted."
16tn (65:7) Heb "I will measure out their pay [from the] beginning into their lap," i.e., he will give them everything they have earned.
17tn (65:8) Heb "just as." In the Hebrew text the statement is one long sentence, "Just as..., so I will do...."
18tn (65:8) Heb "for a blessing is in it."
19tn (65:8) Heb "by not destroying everyone."
20tn (65:9) Heb "it." The third feminine singular pronominal suffix probably refers to the land which contains the aforementioned mountains.
21sn (65:10) Sharon was a plain located to the west, along the Mediterranean coast north of Joppa and south of Carmel.
22sn (65:10) The Valley of Achor ("Achor" means "trouble" in Hebrew) was the site of Achan's execution. It was located to the east, near Jericho.
23tn (65:10) Heb "a resting place for cattle."
24tn (65:10) Heb "for my people who seek me."
25tn (65:11) The Hebrew text has simply, "forget." The words "about worshiping at" are supplied in the translation for clarification.
26tn (65:11) The Hebrew has dgl, "for Gad," the name of a pagan deity. See HALOT 176.
27tn (65:11) The Hebrew has ynml, "for Meni," the name of a pagan deity. See HALOT 602.
28tn (65:12) Heb "I assign you to the sword." Some emend the Qal verb form yt!yn]m*, "I assign," to the Piel yt!yN]m!, " I ordain." The verb sounds like the name of the god Meni (yn]m=), "Destiny; Fate." The soundplay draws attention to the irony of the statement. The sinners among God's people worship the god Meni, apparently in an effort to ensure a bright destiny for themselves. But the LORD is the one who really determines their destiny and he has decreed their demise.
29tn (65:12) Or, "at the slaughter."
30tn (65:12) Heb "that which is evil in my eyes."
31tn (65:14) Heb "from the good of the heart."
32tn (65:14) Heb "from the pain of the heart."
33tn (65:14) Heb "from the breaking of the spirit."
34tn (65:15) Heb "you will leave your name for an oath to my chosen ones."
sn (65:15) For an example of such a curse formula see Jer 29:22.
35tn (65:16) Or, "in the land."
36tn (65:16) Heb "will pronounce a blessing by the God of truth."
37tn (65:16) Or, "in the land."
38tn (65:16) Heb "will take an oath by the God of truth."
39tn (65:16) Heb "for the former distresses will be forgotten, and they will be hidden from my eyes."
40sn (65:17) This hyperbolic statement likens the coming transformation of Jerusalem (see vv. 18-19) to a new creation of the cosmos.
41tn (65:17) Or, perhaps, "things."
42tn (65:17) Heb "and they will not come up on the mind."
43tn (65:18) Heb "Jerusalem, joy." The next verse suggests the meaning: The LORD will create Jerusalem to be a source of joy to himself.
44tn (65:18) Heb "her people, happiness." See the preceding note.
45tn (65:19) Heb "and I will rejoice in Jerusalem, and be happy in my people."
46tn (65:20) Heb "and there will not be from there again a nursing infant of days," i.e., one that lives just a few days.
47tn (65:20) Heb "or an old [man] who does not fill out his days."
48tn (65:20) Heb "for the child as a son of one hundred years will die." The point seems to be that those who die at the age of a hundred will be considered children, for the average life span will be much longer than that. The category "child" will be redefined in light of the expanded life spans that will characterize this new era.
49tn (65:20) Heb "the one who misses." afj is used here in its basic sense of "miss the mark." See HALOT 305. Another option is to translate, "and the sinner who reaches the age of a hundred will be cursed."
50tn (65:22) Heb "they will not build, and another live [in it]."
51tn (65:22) Heb "they will not plant, and another eat."
52tn (65:22) Heb "for like the days of the tree [will be] the days of my people."
53tn (65:22) Heb "the work of their hands."
54tn (65:23) Heb "and they will not give birth to horror."
55tn (65:23) Heb "for offspring blessed by the LORD they [will be], and their descendants along with them."
56sn (65:25) A similar statement appears in 11:6.
57sn (65:25) These words also appear in 11:7.
58sn (65:25) Some see an allusion to Gen 3:14 (note "you will eat dirt"). The point would be that even in this new era the snake (often taken as a symbol of Satan) remains under God's curse. However, it is unlikely that such an allusion exists. Even if there is an echo of Gen 3:14, the primary allusion is to 11:8, where snakes are pictured as no longer dangerous. They will no longer attack other living creatures, but will be content to crawl along the ground. (The statement "you will eat dirt" in Gen 3:14 means "you will crawl on the ground." In the same way the statement "dirt will be its food" in Isa 65:25 means "it will crawl on the ground.")
59tn (65:25) Heb "in all my holy mountain." These same words appear in 11:9. See the note there.
sn (65:25) As in 11:1-9 the prophet anticipates a time when the categories predator-prey no longer exist. See the note at the end of 11:8.
1tn (66:2) Heb "all these." The phrase refers to the heavens and earth, mentioned in the previous verse.
2tn (66:2) Heb "and all these were." Some prefer to emend wyhyw, "and they were," to wyh ylw, "and to me they were," i.e., "and they belong to me."
3tn (66:2) Heb "and to this one I look."
4tn (66:2) Heb "to the humble and the lowly in spirit and the one who trembles at my words."
5tn (66:3) Heb "one who slaughters a bull, one who strikes down a man." Some understand a comparison here and in the following lines. In God's sight the one who sacrifices is like (i.e., regarded as) a murderer or one whose worship is ritually defiled or idolatrous. The translation above assumes that the language is not metaphorical, but descriptive of the sinners' hypocritical behavior. (Note the last two lines of the verse, which suggests they are guilty of abominable practices.) On the one hand, they act pious and offer sacrifices; but at the same time they commit violent crimes against men, defile their sacrifices, and worship other gods.
6tn (66:3) Heb "one who sacrifices a lamb, one who breaks a dog's neck." Some understand a comparison, but see the previous note.
sn (66:3) The significance of breaking a dog's neck is uncertain, though the structure of the statement when compared to the preceding and following lines suggests the action is viewed in a negative light. According to Exod 13:13 and 34:20, one was to "redeem" a firstborn donkey by offering a lamb; if one did not "redeem" the firstborn donkey in this way, then its neck must be broken. According to Deut 21:1-9 a heifer's neck was to be broken as part of the atonement ritual to purify the land from the guilt of bloodshed. It is not certain if these passages relate in any way to the action described in Isa 66:3.
7tn (66:3) Heb "one who offers an offering, pig's blood." Some understand a comparison, but see the note at the end of the first line.
8tn (66:3) Heb "one who offers incense as a memorial offering, one who blesses something false." Some understand a comparison, but see the note at the end of the first line. /wa, which has a wide variety of attested nuances, here refers metonymically to an idol. See HALOT 22 and BDB 20.
9tn (66:3) Heb "also they have chosen their ways."
10tn (66:3) Heb "their being [or, "soul"] takes delight in their disgusting [things]."
11tn (66:4) The precise meaning of the noun is uncertain. It occurs only here and in 3:4 (but see the note there). It appears to be derived from the verbal root, llu, which can carry the nuance, "deal severely."
12tn (66:4) Heb "that which is evil in my eyes."
13tn (66:5) Heb "who tremble at his word."
14tn (66:5) Heb "brothers."
15tn (66:5) Or, "so that we might witness your joy." The point of this statement is unclear.
16tn (66:8) Heb "land," but here Jra stands metonymically for an organized nation (see the following line).
17sn (66:9) The rhetorical questions expect the answer, "Of course not!"
18tn (66:11) Or, "in order that."
19tn (66:11) Heb "you will suck and be satisfied, from her comforting breast."
20tn (66:11) Heb "you will slurp and refresh yourselves from her heavy breast."
sn (66:11) Zion's residents will benefit from and enjoy her great material prosperity. See v. 12.
21tn (66:12) Heb "Look, I am ready to extend to her like a river prosperity [or, "peace"], and like an overflowing stream, the riches of nations."
22tn (66:12) The words "from her breast" are supplied in the translation for clarification (see v. 11).
23tn (66:13) Heb "like a man whose mother comforts him."
24tn (66:14) "and you will see and your heart will be happy."
25tn (66:14) Heb "and your bones like grass will sprout."
26tn (66:14) Heb "and the hand of the LORD will be made known to his servants, and anger to his enemies."
27sn (66:15) Chariots are like a windstorm in their swift movement and in the way that they kick up dust.
28tn (66:15) Heb "to cause to return with the rage of his anger, and his battle cry [or, "rebuke"] with flames of fire."
29tn (66:16) Heb "flesh."
30tn (66:16) Heb "many are the slain of the LORD."
31tn (66:17) Heb "the ones who consecrate themselves and the ones who purify themselves toward the orchards [or, "gardens"] after the one in the midst." The precise meaning of the statement is unclear, though it is obvious that some form of idolatry is in view.
32tn (66:17) Heb "ones who eat the flesh of the pig and the disgusting thing and the mouse."
33tn (66:17) Heb "together they will come to an end."
34tc (66:18) The Hebrew text reads literally, "and I, their deeds and their thoughts, am coming." The syntax here is very problematic, suggesting that the text may have suffered corruption. Some suggest that the words "their deeds and their thoughts" have been displaced from v. 16. The feminine form hab should probably be emended to the masculine ab, for the LORD is speaking here.
35tn (66:18) Heb "and the tongues."
36tn (66:19) Heb "and I will set a sign among them." The precise meaning of this statement is unclear. Elsewhere "to set a sign" means "perform a mighty act" (Ps 78:43; Jer 32:20), "make [someone] an object lesson" (Ezek 14:8), and "erect a [literal] standard" (Ps 74:4).
37tn (66:19) Some prefer to read "Put" (i.e., Libya).
38sn (66:19) That is, Lydia (in Asia Minor).
39tn (66:19) Heb "drawers of the bow."
40sn (66:19) That is, Greece.
41tn (66:19) Or, "islands."
42tn (66:20) Heb "brothers."
43tn (66:20) The words "they will bring them" are supplied in the translation for stylistic reasons.
44tn (66:20) The precise meaning of this word is uncertain. Some suggest it refers to "chariots." See HALOT 498.
45tn (66:23) Heb "new moon."
46tn (66:23) Heb "flesh."
47tn (66:23) Or, "bow down before."
48tn (66:24) Heb "for their worm will not die."
49tn (66:24) Heb "and their fire will not be extinguished."
50tn (66:24) Heb "and they will be an abhorrence to all flesh."
sn (66:24) This verse depicts a huge mass burial site where the seemingly endless pile of maggot-infested corpses are being burned.
